### Post by mark202 on 2015-03-03
Ok Guys, first time using anything but windows as an OS.  Decided to turn the computer into a HTPC and found ubuntu and xbmc as well.  Found out that in order for me to use the HDMI to transmit audio I need to set my audio to run through HDMI.  So I have attempted to download AMD Catalyst to assit with this issue.  I downloaded the fglrx-amdcccle before I downloaded and installed Synaptic Package Manager.  I think I did something with fglrx-amdcccle and stuffed it up so now I have issues.
Issue 1: I mark the program for installation and get this error [I][B]Could not apply changes!
Fix broken packages first.

[/B][/I]I then try and use Synaptic to fix broken package and get the attached error.  I have tried the update - upgrade and so forth to fix it but nothing seems to be happening.  I then try the remove command to get rid of the dependencies and end up with this error

E: Could not get lock /var/lib/dpkg/lock - open (11: Resource temporarily unavailable)
E: Unable to lock the administration directory (/var/lib/dpkg/), is another process using it?

Can someone please help

---

### Post by kerry_s on 2015-03-03
close all other package programs, only 1 can run at a time.
in terminal:
sudo apt-get -f install
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get upgrade

i put them all to separate commands just in case theres something wrong, just run 1 at a time.

---

### Post by Bucky Ball on 2015-03-03
You don't need catalyst or third-party drivers for HDMI. What you have on the laptop monitor is what you will get on the attached monitor. I suggest uninstalling what you've installed, then:

```
sudo apt-get autoremove
sudo apt-get update
sudo apt-get upgrade
sudo apt-get dist-upgrade
```

Please report any and all errors.

---

### Post by mark202 on 2015-03-03

### Post by mark202 on 2015-03-03

### Post by Bucky Ball on 2015-03-03
Install Pulseaudio Volume Control if not already installed (pavucontrol, when you can get to a desktop and things are back to normal). That will let you route the audio to whatever you want.

As far as I know, Catalyst is for the video.

---

### Post by ajgreeny on 2015-03-03
So far nobody has asked you what hardware you are using which could have a great bearing on what you need to do, particularly with regard to the catalyst graphics driver.

Let's see the output of command **lspci** for a start and go from there.

### Post by mark202 on 2015-03-03
